  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b9cf727d-9ffb-4a1b-a7bc-64a0b63526e0'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText5104846859197318926" style="display:none"><i>Beware of the woods and the dark, dank deep.<br /><br />He’ll follow you home, and he won’t let you sleep.</i><br /><br />Who are the Sawkill Girls?<br /><br />Marion: the new girl. Awkward and plain, steady and dependable. Weighed down by tragedy and hungry for love she’s sure she’ll never find.<br /><br />Zoey: the pariah. Luckless and lonely, hurting but hiding it. Aching with grief and dreaming of vanished girls. Maybe she’s broken—or maybe everyone else is.<br /><br />Val: the queen bee. Gorgeous and privileged, ruthless and regal. Words like silk and eyes like knives, a heart made of secrets and a mouth full of lies.<br /><br />Their stories come together on the island of Sawkill Rock, where gleaming horses graze in rolling pastures and cold waves crash against black cliffs. Where kids whisper the legend of an insidious monster at parties and around campfires.<br /><br />Where girls have been disappearing for decades, stolen away by a ravenous evil no one has dared to fight… until now.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2559212223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17487411415844649304">Wow. The fact that lights didn't start flickering ominously and the trees weren't shaking and clattering in the wind and gusty voices weren't rattling off the walls and grating my ears while I was reading this book is supremely upsetting and not at all excellent if you ask me...<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br/><br/><strong>Marion Althouse</strong> arrives in the small town of Sawkill Rock with her mother and sister, Charlotte, hoping that the move would lessen the ache of their loss, now that they have to make </span>
  <span id="freeText17487411415844649304" style="display:none">Wow. The fact that lights didn't start flickering ominously and the trees weren't shaking and clattering in the wind and gusty voices weren't rattling off the walls and grating my ears while I was reading this book is supremely upsetting and not at all excellent if you ask me...<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>Marion Althouse</strong> arrives in the small town of Sawkill Rock with her mother and sister, Charlotte, hoping that the move would lessen the ache of their loss, now that they have to make do with the broken bits of themselves that their father has left behind. Instead, Marion soon discovers that the island’s inoffensive exterior is but a pearled shell that holds a fear so dark it has become as much a part of the island as the woods and nails and rot. Something is very, very wrong in Sawkill Rock, and it’s made manifest when Charlotte disappears—her loss, like a scythe, cutting the strings that were holding Marion upright.<br /><br /><strong>Zoey Harlow</strong>, the police Chief’s daughter, would never be free of the past, never able to turn and face forward until she finds out what happened to her best friend Thora who has similarly vanished. Her restless mining for answers leads Zoey to a jarring reality: girls have been disappearing in Sawkill Rock for decades and nobody seems to care. Zoey refuses to let the blood of all these girls—with all the potential in the world—spill into nothingness. And <strong>Val Mortimer</strong> gives her a place to put all the blame and fury she’s been carrying all this time.<br /><br />The Mortimer women have bought their wealth and power with all the nameless girls they’d fed to The Collector in the years since they’d let it crawl down their throats and take up residence inside their bellies. For some, the island’s own personal bogeyman may be nothing more than a rumor that time has smoothed down to the shape of a myth, but to Val Mortimer, The Collector is as real as the blood she pays him like a tithe to keep him silent.<br /><br />Three girls, three wills: one to summon the monster, and two to bar his way. All is blown open, and the truth spills out like blood.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls. All of them Sawkill girls.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />From startling insights to dizzyingly visual prose to tremendous character work to earnest approaches to identity, gender and sexuality, there's honestly so much more than I can feasibly talk about here.<br /><br /><em>Sawkill Girls</em> is a moody, atmospheric story that leaves a strong impression that will not wane anytime soon. It’s as sharp as a dagger and cold as a corpse. Claire LeGrand evokes her setting with tactile immediacy and deft skill, and while Sawkill Rock is an imaginary place, it still feels solidly real. She twists the most mundane scenarios into something dark and sinister, and, like the night has a way of lending weight to phantasms, the author’s words full of meaning and her descriptions brimming with potential and vibrant life make the whole alive with brutal intensity. <strong>I absolutely loved it.</strong><br /><br />But the real magic with <em>Sawkill Girls</em> lies with the subversions and nuances that LeGrand so craftily weaves into her yarn. Bold and illuminating, this story, which has the unmistakable shape of a dark fairy tale with the rich density of horror, centers around three young women who, all, have lost something to the monster: Marion—her sister, Zoey—her best friend, and Val—her freedom.<br /><br /><em>Sawkill Girls</em> forces the reader to see its characters as more than their actions. <strong>Val’s character, in particular, is utterly mesmerizing.</strong> There’s a kind of stirring, an allure about her that creeps over you, and when LeGrand begins to peel away the shell around her, what we see is not exactly pretty. The Mortimer women are more a personification of hundreds of years of fear and complicity than living, breathing human beings. Every Mortimer daughter is a gift to be given—or more like livestock to be sold to the monster in the woods. This is all Val has ever known. The monster willed, and she obeyed. And the part of me that couldn't reconcile with that sort of seemingly pitiless cruelty warried constantly with the part that understood that Val is a victim too.<br /><br />But Val's victimhood pales in view of the collateral damage that she contributes in, and the story does not allow Val to slough off her culpability for serving the monster, even if she was forced to her knees to do it. Then, <strong>Val falls in love with Marion</strong> and the carefully cultivated detachment and unconditional obedience that has been rammed down her throat for years cede their spot for gasping gnaws of panic and a heart-wrenching awareness of what she has done…and that’s where our perception of Val starts to reform itself into a new shape. Val's arc is truly one of my favorite things about this book.<br /><br />And since we're on the subject of favorite things, it’s no secret—in the way the moon is no secret—that I can’t help but always hold stories centered around women's relationships to each other to a higher standard. <em>Sawkill Girls</em> triumphs on several fronts, but it’s <strong>its careful and genuine depiction of female friendships</strong> that made this book leap and claim a spot amongst my favorite books of this year.<br /><br />There are forces—that I’ll abstain from mentioning because <em>spoilers</em>—that attempted to pit Val, Marion and Zoey against each other, that prodded at their differences with a degree of enthusiasm that bordered on the obscene, hoping the rift between them would become a chasm. But Marion, Val and Zoey stood side by side, braced against the future—forgotten, in their determination, is all the strife between them—when they begun to recognize the power of putting their voices together against a system that strived to bully out their last defiant shred of hope.<br /><br /><em>Sawkill Girls</em> has pretty much taken the "girl-on-girl hate" trope and smashed it against the wall. It felt very resonant in its portrayal of the misogyny that’s embedded in a culture that perpetuate the misguided notion that women are socialized to resent other women. While rivalries occur between any genders, we, unfortunately, live in a society that seems to encourage women to tear each other down for no reason other than lucrative gain and enticing drama. This is displayed all the time in social media with articles and posts that attempt to create a vicious competition—that isn’t there and should never be—between women who were all successful and brilliant and magnificent in their own right and are probably not plotting each other’s downfall.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Girls hunger. And we’re taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn’t enough food for us all.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I also relished this book’s diversity and careful exploration of sexual identity—Marion is bisexual, Val is also queer (but no label was used), Zoey is black and asexual and has broken up with her boyfriend, Grayson, because she thinks her asexuality would be an issue (IT ISN’T! This boy would drag his ravaged body across the universe for her, okay?) Speaking of Grayson, it frankly feels so subversive to have a male lead who’s more than content taking on the responsibility of cleaning and baking and translating ambiguous latin texts, while the female leads determinedly take on the world, adventuring with minimal reservations, and trailing wreckage in their wake. What a power move.<br /><br />Overall, I know that, objectively speaking, existing in this world would be maximally dreadful, but the concept of belonging to <strong>a group of SAPPHIC GIRLS who draw on their magical powers to FUCK UP the life of the island’s bogeyman</strong> is firmly inside my circle of interests. I’m left with the overwhelming desire to stand in the middle of a circle that I've drawn using my blood on the top of a mountain during a full moon, summon a demon to slay it, perform at least one exorcism and take down a cult. And make some friends, too, I guess.<br /><br />Seriously, <strong>READ THIS BOOK</strong>.<br /><br /><a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/runawaywithdreamthieves" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> | <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">TUMBLR</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17487411415844649304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2358313631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358313631" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358313631?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358313631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15491927697739744868"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541880217i/26575313._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls. All of them Sawkill girls.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Sawkill Girls</i> is going to be such an amazing, atmospheric, spooky Halloween read for so many. The start of this book was phenomenal, and the first half was five star worthy in my opinion. I just, didn’t love the ending of this, but I think many of you will. And overall, I completely recommend this, </span>
  <span id="freeText15491927697739744868" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541880217i/26575313._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls. All of them Sawkill girls.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Sawkill Girls</i> is going to be such an amazing, atmospheric, spooky Halloween read for so many. The start of this book was phenomenal, and the first half was five star worthy in my opinion. I just, didn’t love the ending of this, but I think many of you will. And overall, I completely recommend this, and I had such an amazing time reading this creepy tale. <br><br>Sawkill Island has never been safe for young girls. More and more frequently young girls have gone missing, without their bodies ever being found. There is a local legend about a paranormal beast called The Collector, who hunts and feasts on these young girls, while simultaneously growing stronger himself. But we also soon find out, there is no way that the Collector is capturing these girls on his own. <br><br>We are introduced to three girls, whose stories and fates interweave, regardless of what they have to say about it. And only these three girls have the power to save the island. That is, if they are willing to come together and try. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A girl with incredible strength. A girl who can vanish. A girl who burns.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Zoey</b>
</u> - Black, bi (not on page but stated attraction to boys and girls), and asexual. Also, such a damn blessing. Recently lost her best friend to the tragedy of the island. Her father is the local sheriff. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Marion</b>
</u> - Plus sized, likes girls, but I don’t believe Lesbian, pan, bi, or any other label is said or implied. But she does start a relationship with a girl in this book (and holy shit, it’s so good)! She is also dealing with the loss of her father, while trying to be the support system for her mother and her sister while they move to this island. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Val</b>
</u> - Queen bee of the island and hiding a dark secret that she shares with her family. Also, her sexuality is never stated on page, but she talks about relationships with boys and has a relationship with a girl. <br><br>Honorable mention and honorary fourth member:<br>➽ <u>
  <b>Grayson</b>
</u> - Zoey’s best friend and ex. My favorite character in the entire book. I would honestly die for this boy. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Tragedy had touched Sawkill, again and again and again, but after each girl’s disappearance, once a respectable amount of time had passed, everyone seemed to stop caring.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>These three girls come together and try to figure out what is killing these girls and if there is anyway to stop it from happening to them. At first, this book feels like you’re reading it through a fog, where you aren’t sure what exactly is going on. But mystery after mystery is eventually answered, and a beautiful tale of friendship, womanhood, and love is unfolded. I mean, it is unfolded after and during some really dark, gory, and violent scenes. This is for sure a horror book. <br><br>I really want to emphasize that this is a dark book. Please use caution and make sure you are in the right mindset while reading. <b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for loss of a loved one, somewhat detailed murders, violence, gore, a lot of talk of blood, grief, abuse, parental abuse, underage drinking, talk of miscarrying, sexual abuse (unwanted kissing, and maybe touching), animal death, scene with a girl purposely cutting open her palm, use of the word “fat’ negatively, and a really acephobic comment that is completely challenged and apologized for (but I know that it can still be really hurtful to read). <br><br>And just to talk a bit more about it, <i>Sawkill Girls</i> centers around grief, trauma, and loss. It also heavily talks about how we are not the mistakes or the problems of our parents, even though they could heavily impact our own lives. Each girl has their own heartache. Marion, being forced to keep her mother and sister safe after losing their father, while never allowing herself to grieve. Zoey, for learning how to live after pushing someone who loves you away and after losing your best friend. Val, for struggling to please her mother, while being abused by her mother, while never being able to leave her mother.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There was a magnetism to the Mortimer women, and they knew it, and they used it. It was their right, this witchery; they’d given up their souls for it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And Claire Legrand is blessing us with sexual representation in this book. Not only do we have a swoon worthy f/f romance that I was so there for from the very start, but she also gives us the best asexuality representation I’ve read in a book to date! And the word asexuality is used on page, the stigmas and stereotypes are discussed very thoughtfully, and my heart is so full. Also, full disclosure: I do not ID on the ace spectrum, but I did at one point in my life. <br><br>This story also heavily discusses how girls are raised in a world that is constantly pitting us against one another. How this competitiveness is instilled in our blood, and bones, and very being by society. How men make gross jokes like “this is why girls can't work together” and other disgusting comments along those lines, because it helps reinforce these stereotypes. How we are born to waste time trying to raise ourselves above other girls, when we could come together and raise each other up equally. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Girls hunger. And we’re taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn’t enough food for us all.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And this story is so very feminist, and Claire weaves the undertones, flawlessly, in every scene. I mean, this is a story about three girls, from very different backgrounds, all harboring their own individual pains and hurts, coming together to defeat a monster. But it is also about how we view girls as both the most vulnerable prey, but also the most sacrificable objects. And how if a problem doesn’t impact white, cis, dudes, the problem isn’t going to gain priority to get fixed. <br><br>I won’t lie, and I said it above, but I didn’t love the ending of this book, but (just like reading) I think it will be subjective. I was really hoping for a certain ending, and I was a little disappointed when it didn’t come to fruition. I also wasn’t in love with The Collector. I mean, you’re not supposed to be in love with him, but once we learned more about him, I just wasn’t impressed. Which, again, is why I think I fell so in love with the first half of this book, because the mystery surrounding him was so good! <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed this standalone! Also, at this point, I think I’ll just preorder what Claire Legrand does next, because she’s an author that just keeps impressing me, and my queer self. Seriously, the sexuality representation in this book is such a blessing. Also, there is a moth that reminds me of Sarai, and I felt personally attacked in the best way possible. I love the entire vibe and aesthetic of this book, and I truly think it’s going to have such an impressive impact come October! <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br>❤ Buddy Read with: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13507409-amy" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14843185.Julie_Zantopoulos" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17590369-imogen-gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Imogen</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellie</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35673299-laura-yamin" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68321894-natasha" rel="nofollow noopener">Natasha</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42780417-wren-wrensreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Wren</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36907106-alexis-theslothreader" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexis</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15491927697739744868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2332944407" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2332944407?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sapphic-books-shelf">sapphic-books-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-tbr-lgbtq">x-tbr-lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332944407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10954978608178154772"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Screw that book,” said Val. “It was written by men.” She held out her free hand to Marion. “We’re rewriting it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>First of all, <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I50gFYnegts' rel='nofollow noopener'>if you wanted to see a Buzzfeed Unsolved investigation into this book, yes, that exists, and there aren't even spoilers</a>. Second of all, this book was a freaking masterpiece and I <i>need</i> you all to read it. <br/><br/><i>Sawkill Girls</i> is a book about not being your parent’s mistake, the deep and long-lasting effects of trauma and loss, and the repression of grief we all go th</span>
  <span id="freeText10954978608178154772" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Screw that book,” said Val. “It was written by men.” She held out her free hand to Marion. “We’re rewriting it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />First of all, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I50gFYnegts" rel="nofollow noopener">if you wanted to see a Buzzfeed Unsolved investigation into this book, yes, that exists, and there aren't even spoilers</a>. Second of all, this book was a freaking masterpiece and I <i>need</i> you all to read it. <br /><br /><i>Sawkill Girls</i> is a book about not being your parent’s mistake, the deep and long-lasting effects of trauma and loss, and the repression of grief we all go through. It’s also a horror book. Also, it’s also about three girls and they’re all sapphic and all so well written and developed I want to cry. <br /><br />I don’t quite know how to describe what made this book so fantastic - it’s a character study that’s also a thriller, a supernatural horror movie that’s also a discussion of grief and trauma. The thematic arc around Zoey’s loss of Thora; Marion’s experience with loss of someone close to her, and her experience of losing her mother’s being fully there, a loss of a loving family that isn’t even full; and Val’s feeling of never having had a loving family, but mourning for the love she’s never gotten nonetheless. It’s just fucking awesome. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽C H A R A C T E R S</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />→Marion - bisexual daughter of a mother in mourning, trying to find her own identity.<br />→Val - morally grey lesbian abuse survivor. <s>if any of you know me you possibly know that this a character archetype written for me, personally,</s><br />→Zoey - black and bi and asexual legend trying to recover from grief over a friend. <br /><br />🌷Val’s character arc and character development is lowkey someone reading my 2015 tumblr posts and being like “okay so what does she like in a morally grey character” she’s Morally Gay™️ and I love her. On a more serious note, I genuinely related a lot to some of her characterization; her ideation around love as something temporal, but her contrasting desire for some kind of real love nonetheless. <br /><br />🌷Zoey... is such an important character to me? god she lets herself be angry about things and the NARRATIVE lets her be angry about things and humanizes her so much and god I love that !!!!!!!!! In all seriousness, it’s really rare for women to be allowed by their narratives to experience <i>angry</i> grief; Zoey is not here to be punished, because even with occasional blips, she is processing her emotions. <br /><br />🌷Marion was actually somewhat my least favorite, but I still absolutely loved reading her chapters, which should definitely say something about how freaking good this book is. I really love the emphasis put on her ability to grow and move past her grief, not putting it in the past but also not making herself into a vehicle for it. And her relationship with her mother, who is not always there for her, was utterly heartbreaking. <br /><br />Despite the fact that they’re not leads, I enjoyed the other characters as well; Zoey’s dad is awesome, and Charlotte was a lot of fun. Perhaps more importantly, Grayson has done nothing wrong ever in his life.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽T H E M A T I C S</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />🌷At its core, this is a book about <b>grief</b>. In their own ways, each character in this book is dealing with what it feels like to mourn, to be alone, to miss people who aren't coming back. For Zoe, it is her ex-best friend. For Marion, it is her father and one other close person. For Val, it is love that she has never had. And their reactions!! are so different!! I think the way grief is handled within this book is so glorious and incredible. <br /><br />🌷We got in on Val!! So let's talk about Val. The arc around <b>commodification of body</b> as experienced by Val is just genuinely.... incredible, and one of my favorite arcs within this book. Val is being preyed upon by a creature who has essentially given her no other choice than to be an accomplice to murder, time and time again — and more than that, she is the daughter of a mother <b>who has never taught her that she has worth.</b> Legrand refuses to shy away from the horror of what Val has gone through and is going through every day, while also not allowing her suffering to outweigh that of others. It's a hard-to-handle real-world issue wrapped up in a horror movie premise, and that is exactly what works so well about this discussion. <br /><br />🌷I really really love <b>how much this focuses on girls.</b> All I can say is the blurb of this as “girls loving girls, girls kissing girls, girls being friends with girls, girls helping girls” was really not pulling its fucking punches, and god this book was what I deserved in the year of our lord 2018. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽A T M O S P H E R E</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />🌷This is one of the most atmospheric books I read in 2018 or like, ever. Actually, no, guys, I should warn you, this book was <b>fucking scary</b>. If any of you have read The Diviners, in all its paranormal reading-this-for-the-characters-but-also-I’m-terrified glory, you will know what this feels like. And don’t worry, the <b>fear factor</b> is not playing around: with one (1) singular exception, this didn’t stray away from the character deaths. <br /><br />🌷I felt Enveloped in this book, and it is because <b>the writing of this book is fucking glorious.</b> This is one of those books that I had to highlight on almost every page. I actually read this backstage, while very stressed out, at a show I was teching for, and it was the only thing that I couldn’t be distracted from. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽R O M A N C E</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />🌷Grayson and Zoey !!!!!!!!!!! Grayson and Zoey Christ the #1 m/f book ship of my entire life god im crying they’re so good and soft<br />Okay, so Grayson and Zoey are best friends who dated and are now exes, and I’m beginning to think I really like the exes-to-getting-back-together dynamic. I like how frank the discussion of relationship insecurities was here; there is no glossing over the issues their relationship had. And by the time anything happens between them, their friendship had already convinced me fully of their platonic-soulmates capacity. (Ironically, I platonically reconnected with my ex on the exact same day I finished this book. What’s happening, @ the universe?)<br /><br />🌷MARION AND VAL !!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! <br />I don’t even know if I’m joking when I say Marion and Val are one of my favorite f/f ships I’ve ever gotten out of a ya book. I sometimes struggle with villain ships, but this dynamic is just <b>so interesting</b>. I absolutely loved how their dynamic evolved and improved over time, and their development made me so happy. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>➽I N C O N C L U S I O N</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I somehow managed to hold it together without crying for this entire book and then I read the last page and the dam broke and I just,,,,,, I don’t even know what to say I can’t review this or think about this it’s too flawlessly catered to my taste on every single level I would give my life for it. I originally titled this review <b>laundry list of reasons this was written specifically for Elise, 17, user @TheBookishActress</b> and honestly… mood. This was so perfect and just what I wanted to close off my 2018. <br /><br />TW: homophobia (challenged), acephobia (challenged), sexual assault, parental abuse, animal death. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>release date:</i>
</b> 11 October 2018<br />✨<i>Arc received from the publisher via Netgalley for an honest review.</i> <br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10954978608178154772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8391041630414615184">Okay. That was disappointing.<br/><br/>This had so much potential and I actually really loved the first third/half. <br/>But it went so hardcore downhill after that.. I don't even really know what to say.<br/><br/>It evolved from a creepy, creative story with great, diverse characters to a way overdone, rushed, man hating mess. <br/>I was so excited for the female empowerment (and I really really loved all the diversity!) but that quickly turned into painting men as the most evil beings on this planet. <br/><br/><br/><br/>I have a few quotes fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8391041630414615184" style="display:none">Okay. That was disappointing.<br /><br />This had so much potential and I actually really loved the first third/half. <br />But it went so hardcore downhill after that.. I don't even really know what to say.<br /><br />It evolved from a creepy, creative story with great, diverse characters to a way overdone, rushed, man hating mess. <br />I was so excited for the female empowerment (and I really really loved all the diversity!) but that quickly turned into painting men as the most evil beings on this planet. <br /><br /><br /><br />I have a few quotes for you:<br /><br /><br />"I feel sort of weird doing this. Like I'm some sort of asshole professor mansplaining the situation to you"<br />- said by the best friend of the person who he is talking to. And he was literally ASKED to explain.<br /><br /><br />"Can I once again apologize on behalf of men everywhere? Because we can really fucking suck sometimes" - "Sometimes?" - "Most of the time" <br />- Ugh. Do I even have to comment on that? <br /><br /><br />"Marion couldn't imagine a God like the one she'd grown up hearing about - some man sitting in the clouds, maneuvering the pieces of the world to suit his whims because he, of course, knows best" <br />- Uhhh.. yeah. I'm not religious but I feel like this might be low key offensive.<br /><br /><br />"Screw that book, it was written by men."<br />Yeah, because everything every man ever creates is shit. <br /><br /><br />Look, I know there are a lot of disgusting shitty man out there and feminism is so so important for our world. But do y'all really think we'll get far with HATING THE OTHER HALF OF THE POPULATION? <br />Ever heard about equality? <br />I might be overreacting or misunderstanding some shit, so please, I'm open for discussion! If you disagree, let me know why :) <br /><br />This whole book had TWO "nice" male characters.<br />I'm not saying every book needs nice male characters to be a good book, definitely not. <br />Hit me with the girl power please. <br />But you could feel how hard this book tried to make you dislike the male gender. It just threw those two in to cover that up lmao like "BUT LOOK NOT ALL MEN ARE BADDDD WE EVEN PUT A NICE ONE IN OUR STORY" ya mhm. Sure. <br /><br />Okay I'm done, sorry for my rant lol. <br /><br />And again, please don't take this the wrong way. I definitely consider myself a feminist. But sorry, I don't hate men. </span>

<div id="review_2544135172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2544135172" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2544135172?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2544135172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7026445496536092988"><i>
  <b>A girl with incredible strength.<br/>A girl who can vanish.<br/>A girl who burns.</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>There are always three.</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548341649ra/26964420.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548021573ra/26948121.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When Marion moves to Sawkill Rock, an island off the coast of Massachusetts, with her mother and older sister, they view it as a place for their family to recover and rebuild. <br/><br/>After the unexpected death of her father, things have been really rough. Marion was left to hold the family together; a weighty responsibility for any teen. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548341649ra/26964421.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Once on island, it doesn't take long for Marion to realize Sawkil</span>
  <span id="freeText7026445496536092988" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>A girl with incredible strength.<br>A girl who can vanish.<br>A girl who burns.</b>
</i><br><br><b>
  <i>There are always three.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548341649ra/26964420.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548021573ra/26948121.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Marion moves to Sawkill Rock, an island off the coast of Massachusetts, with her mother and older sister, they view it as a place for their family to recover and rebuild. <br><br>After the unexpected death of her father, things have been really rough. Marion was left to hold the family together; a weighty responsibility for any teen. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548341649ra/26964421.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Once on island, it doesn't take long for Marion to realize Sawkill isn't going to be all sunshine and rainbows. <br><br>Something ominous lurks upon these shores and it just so happens to be feeding on the blood of young women.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523828008ra/25383013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Zoey, also a transplant to the island with her police officer Dad, is all too familiar with the little problem of disappearing girls plaguing the small island. <br><br>In fact, her best friend is one of the disappeared and she has never been satisfied with the community's response. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588638850ra/29416098.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Zoey befriends Marion and together they begin to work on unveiling the secrets of Sawkill. <br><br>When Marion's older sister, Charlotte, becomes one of the missing, things really start to heat up.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491526339ra/22419424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Val Mortimer is the Queen Bee, the Regina George of Sawkill Rock, if you will. <br><br>She's beautiful, popular, rich, possibly evil and she's got her sights set on Marion.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489788993ra/22250629.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I went into this book with the mistaken belief that it was a YA Contemporary with some elements of Magical Realism.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527210481ra/25592646.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was mistaken. This book is full-on YA Horror! <br><br>Dark secrets, urban legends, a monster feeding on the blood of girls, an uncoordinated band of kids coming together to defeat evil, a F/F relationship, humor, mystery and danger. This book has it all!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460148621ra/18706399.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The atmosphere is hella dark and fully imagined. <br><br>I was completely drawn into life on the rock. As a person who also lives on a small island, 30-miles out to sea, I can say the 'island life rep' was strong. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448761891ra/17185483.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>This would be a great book to pick up in October.</u> I am actually a little sad I didn't get to it then. <br><br>My one critique would be that I felt like this was a tad bit too long. I started getting anxious toward the end and just wanted a conclusion already! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521226143ra/25224886.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think the same story could have been told, and perhaps better served, if about 50-pages had been shaved off. <br><br>But that is 100% my opinion. What the heck do I know anyway?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531736872ra/25980825.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would recommend this to all my Horror-loving friends, or even just friends who like stories with a dark, creepy atmosphere. <br><br>Definitely worth a read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7026445496536092988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror-etc">mystery-thriller-horror-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2595804803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12163369376301656412">It took me two months to read this book.<br/><br/>For two months, I floundered through this. For two months, I forced myself through in eight page chunks. For two months, the Kindle for Mac application was open on my laptop, with the ebook version of this existing somewhere among, like, eighteen podcasts and four tabs with Twitter open and a sh*t ton of articles about obscure pop culture tidbits.<br/><br/>In short: It took me two months to get through this and I almost couldn’t do even that.<br/><br/>There are some books tha</span>
  <span id="freeText12163369376301656412" style="display:none">It took me two months to read this book.<br /><br />For two months, I floundered through this. For two months, I forced myself through in eight page chunks. For two months, the Kindle for Mac application was open on my laptop, with the ebook version of this existing somewhere among, like, eighteen podcasts and four tabs with Twitter open and a sh*t ton of articles about obscure pop culture tidbits.<br /><br />In short: It took me two months to get through this and I almost couldn’t do even that.<br /><br />There are some books that have no excuse to be boring. Some stories have such excellent synopses and concepts that they should be literally incapable of being anything but a nonstop thrill ride. This book, which centers around an island where a monster is killing girls, and so a gang of girls kill the monster and also the girls are in love, should be nothing other than exciting at every moment. There is not so much as a word of that idea that I am not interested in, or, dare I say, ENTHRALLED BY.<br /><br />And yet, not for a single moment was this book anything but boring to me. Boring boring boring. A punishment to get through. Inexplicably monotonous in a nightmarish way. <br /><br />For a while, this book was fully inescapable on Goodreads. Everyone was reading it and talking about it and loving (? maybe) it, and because I very much enjoy hopping on bandwagons, I TBRed it. Without actually reading that glorious synopsis. And I started reading it also without doing that. <br /><br />At a certain point, I was so confused by what this was supposed to be (okay, approximately 3% of the way in) that I read the synopsis. And I got re-excited!<br /><br />And then I got disappointed again. Because very little of this book is monster-fighting. A lot of it is weird, stylized, strangely descriptive writing that I did not enjoy. And characters I did not care for or understand. And a very slow-moving plot that comes to its climax so late that I did not give half a sh*t by that point.<br /><br />By that point, I was just thrilled to be mere pages away by being done with it forever.<br /><br />Bottom line: The best part of this book, for me, was far and away when it was finally, mercifully over.<br /><br />-----------<br /><br />i finished this book yesterday and was so profoundly bored by the whole thing that i legitimately forgot that i finished it. i just promptly deleted it from my brain.<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />-----------<br /><br />i don't know what's happening but i DO know i don't really care<br /><br />-----------<br /><br />reading this book with no real idea of what it's about. what can I say -- I live on the edge<br /><br />-----------<br /><br />I saw enough people I follow reading this book and talking about this book and TBRing this book that I am right now adding it without even reading the synopsis in full.<br /><br />I know what you're thinking. "If your friends jumped off a cliff would you jump too," blah blah blah, and the answer is yeah, duh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12163369376301656412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2358316730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358316730" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358316730?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fat-rep">fat-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358316730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6356729341168177938">This is one of those reviews that I had to sit on for a while, because I had so many things I wanted to say about this book, and I just couldn’t quite figure out how to condense them into anything even remotely resembling a sensible length of review. <i>Sawkill Girls</i> is being marketed fairly heavily as horror, but it’s fabulism, too, with a world so gorgeously complex that I can’t ever quite determine if I adore it or am terrified of it. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b><i>Come for a while,</i> reads the sign at Sawkill’s ferry dock, </b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6356729341168177938" style="display:none">This is one of those reviews that I had to sit on for a while, because I had so many things I wanted to say about this book, and I just couldn’t quite figure out how to condense them into anything even remotely resembling a sensible length of review. <i>Sawkill Girls</i> is being marketed fairly heavily as horror, but it’s fabulism, too, with a world so gorgeously complex that I can’t ever quite determine if I adore it or am terrified of it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b><i>Come for a while,</i> reads the sign at Sawkill’s ferry dock, <i>and stay forever.</i></b>
</blockquote><br />At Sawkill Rock, the beauty of the island masks a terrible, dark secret: girls keep going missing, and they’re being lost more frequently every year. Nobody knows where they go, and it’s almost become an accepted status quo among the people of the island. The atmosphere of Sawkill Rock is one of the most immersive settings I’ve ever read; I felt transported so fully into the island’s grasp that I couldn’t help the dread worsening in my gut with every chapter’s passing. Claire Legrand’s writing voice is superb here—having read previous work by her, I genuinely believe that <i>this</i> is where she is meant to be.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b><i>My little rock,</i> her mother would say. <i>My grave little mountain.</i></b>
</blockquote><br />There are three main characters to this story, with chapters alternating between their perspectives, and my favorite was Marion, who broke my heart over and over again with the loss of her loved ones and, consequentially, her slackening grasp on normality. The representation in this entire book is amazing, and Marion is <b>bisexual and fat,</b> which is a combination I’ll never tire of (because, hello, it’s me!). These facts are dropped so casually that there’s no room for argument—there is no homophobia or body hatred, despite an occasional very brief moment of self-consciousness on Marion’s part. Beyond her appearance and sexuality, Marion is so tough, and pragmatic, and determined to keep up a strong front. I’ve always been the same way, and so, I constantly saw myself mirrored back in her character.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b><i>Don’t lose yourself to him, my darling one,</i> Sylvia Mortimer had said. <i>Not all of you. Keep a morsel for yourself.</i></b>
</blockquote><br />Though it took me a little longer to warm up to Val Mortimer, I grew fond of her, too. She first appears as this over-simplified “queen bee” persona, but we quickly get to see a side of her that’s so much darker and more haunted than anything you’d imagine (and she’s <b>queer</b>, though we don’t know what her label is). There are quotes in her chapters that have haunted me since the moment I finished this book, and you should be warned that her perspectives frequently depict <b>suicidal ideation</b> and <b>abuse</b>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Zoey’s laugh was bitter. “Oh, and we poor delicate girls are vulnerable and desperate, is that what you’re saying?”</b>
</blockquote><br />Finally, there’s Zoey, who is <b>black and asexual</b> (on page—there’s an entire facet to her back story revolving around this aspect of her life), and even more than that, she’s so determined and stubborn and absolutely lovable despite being a fairly “unlikable” character. She’s stern and feisty, and while I’m not sure if she will be everyone’s cup of tea, I was delighted by her antics and unpredictability.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>It did not relish tying an innocent to the burden of its ancient might. But the Rock required an infantry.</b>
</blockquote><br />Okay… I lied, sort of. There’s a fourth character, but it’s hard to explain. The Rock gets the occasional perspective chapter, and while they’re incredibly short and typically entirely vague, they may have been my absolute favorites. These passages read so lyrically and they are so incredibly haunting. I’ve never read a book where a <i>place</i> was given a thinking, feeling sentience to this degree, and it adds the most amazing layer to the story.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“What I’m saying is that girls hunger. And we’re taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn’t enough food for us all.”</b>
</blockquote><br />On top of the beautiful cast of characters and the haunting atmosphere, this story is so feminist, so empowering and bold and unapologetic. I can’t tell you how strongly this parallels the real world and the ways society casts teen girls aside, nor can I describe how badly I wish I’d had this story as a teen—a story to tell me that it’s okay to be strong, and angry, and queer, and brave, and in need of another mountain to lean on.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>You are mighty. <i>You are one, and one, and one.</i><br />You are fragile. <i>You can move mountains.</i><br />You are breakable. <i>You will never break.</i><br />This power is mine. <i>And now it is yours, too.</i></b>
</blockquote><br />I know I said I’d keep this to a reasonable length, and I’m trying, but <i>Sawkill Girls</i> is one of those stories that I feel has changed me in a way. 2018 has been the year of brilliant, fiercely feminist reads for me, and this one easily joins the ranks of my favorites. I want everyone and anyone I know to pick up a copy of this gorgeous, spooky little book, because it packs such a punch, and I only hope that it will get even <i>half</i> of the hype it deserves.<br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to Katherine Tegen Books for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/09/07/sawkill-girls/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6356729341168177938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2568174970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568174970" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568174970?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568174970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1187602687943498927"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541439956ra/26550860.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Little fairy girl, skipping down the sea <br/>Little fairy girl, pretty as can be <br/>Who is the fellow with the bright clean grin? <br/>Do you want, fairy girl, to weave a spell for him? </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>When Marion, her mother and her sister arrive in Sawkill they hear about the missing girl, Thora. <br/>They hear about the strange and creepy forest full of darkness and danger. <br/>They meet Zoey who hates Val Mortimer more than anyone and anything, because Zoey is sure that Val has something to do with the disappea</span>
  <span id="freeText1187602687943498927" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541439956ra/26550860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Little fairy girl, skipping down the sea <br>Little fairy girl, pretty as can be <br>Who is the fellow with the bright clean grin? <br>Do you want, fairy girl, to weave a spell for him? </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>When Marion, her mother and her sister arrive in Sawkill they hear about the missing girl, Thora. <br>They hear about the strange and creepy forest full of darkness and danger. <br>They meet Zoey who hates Val Mortimer more than anyone and anything, because Zoey is sure that Val has something to do with the disappearance of her former best friend Thora. But Val is the popular beautiful girl with many friends but also many secrets. <br>Soon another girl is missing, but this time something is different. <br>This time Zoey finds Marion in the darkness and they realize that something is going on on this island. Something dark and dangerous. And they need to stop it. <br>When I started this book I didn’t read a summary or a review. I just started to read it. <br>That’s why I thought this would be a story about a girl gone missing, her best friend who searches for her and the new girl that helps her. <br>But I was so wrong. This story is filled with mystery, secrets, sexual tension and a frightening darkness. <br>It was absolutely refreshing and entertaining. And I really loved it. <br><br>Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I love it when a book is filled with strong women that know their value, their strengths but also their weaknesses. <br>And this book was full of them. <br>Marion - the quiet, strong and fearless daughter, sister and friend, who would sacrifice herself for the good of others. <br>Zoey - a smart and wild force. A girl that knows to trust her gut, to never lose your thoughts and dreams to others and who can connect the hints and dots around her faster that anyone.<br>And Val - a beautiful, popular girl who seems to live the perfect life. Until we realize that the things that seem so perfect are actually an absolute horror. <br>Each of them had a background story, a personality and her own confusing thoughts.<br>And what can I say? <br>I fell in love with this girls.<br>Also there was Grayson - cinnamon roll and my newly found perfect book-boyfriend. <br>He’s a feminist, who loves to have a tidy house and who doesn’t care about anything people talk about. He doesn’t care that the some (weird) people say that his girlfriend has to love sex. That his girlfriend can’t be asexual. <br>But he says “f*ck it”. He’s so in love with Zoey with all his heart that he doesn’t care about any bullshit they say. He loves her and he wants to be with her. <br>He’s so freaking cute, I loved him so much. <br>He was so brave for her, so in love with her and such a loving and caring gentleman. <br>Ugh, perfect book boyfriend. ♥️<br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>When we look at the stars we hope that somewhere far away there may be another universe. <br>Something full of light. <br>Something full of magic. <br>But if there is magic and light, there is always danger and darkness. <br>There needs to be a balance. <br>But sometimes monsters from this far away universe find their way to our world.<br>They find a family, a host - desperate people that seek happiness, power or just something good to hold on to. <br>So he makes a deal with them, they get what their hearts desire, but they will obey the beast until it’s free of his bonds. <br>And so the hosts help the beast feed, blood is spread upon the earth. <br>And the earth, the sea, the rocks see that there are horrible things happening on his grounds. <br>So he shares his power with a few selected girls. Powerful extraordinary girls. <br>And with their help he will try to eliminate the beast. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>You know what i really love about our age and our generation? We’re so open up. <br>We don’t care who other people love, we don’t care how we love or if we love someone. <br>We don’t care if their bisexual, homosexual, asexual, transgender or whatever. <br>We accept the people for who they are. <br>Three different girls who’re not only separated by looks but also by something else. <br>One is bisexual, one homosexual and one is asexual. <br>And that was so freakin awesome. <br>I haven’t read any good diverse book in a long time. And that book is now one of my favorite diversity books on my shelves. <br>The way we get to experience the sexuality of this women - the insecurity, the thoughts, the fear. <br>And you know what I love even more?<br>Strong friendship in a book. <br>People that know that sometimes we need to accept, forgive, forget. We need to see that we need each other no matter what. <br>That together we’re stronger, we’re unstoppable and we’re not alone.<br>And I loved the friendship in this book so much.<br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ <br>The story is told in three - maybe three and a half POVs. Marion, Val, Zoey and sometimes a glimpse of the thoughts of the rock. <br>Sometimes we see bits of the past, story’s that are told, songs that were made up. <br>We get to know the girls one by one and we see how they get together, how they hate, fight, talk and love. We experience all their thoughts and feelings in a beautiful opened up way. <br>I really liked the way the story was told. In some way it made you even more interested, sometimes it made you smile and sometimes you felt like you read a horror book. <br>But all in all it was a really refreshing and enjoyable experience and I can definitely recommend the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1187602687943498927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2408535329" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408535329" />
    <a title="Camila Roy ••RoyIsReading••" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40788320-camila-roy-royisreading"><img alt="Camila Roy ••RoyIsReading••" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532282247p2/40788320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408535329?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camila Roy ••RoyIsReading••" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camila Roy ••RoyIsReading••" href="/user/show/40788320-camila-roy-royisreading">Camila Roy ••RoyIsReading••</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40788320-camila-roy-royisreading?shelf=books-i-disliked-hated">books-i-disliked-hated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408535329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11859879236823865533">RATING: 2.75 rounded up to 3/5 <br/><br/>Let me start by saying that I LOVE horror. Spooky, creepy and bizarre is my aesthetic. Supernatural shows are my thing; I can't get enough of them. So, when I read this book's synopsis I was definitely intrigued. Plus, <b>Claire Legrand</b> is the author (she wrote <i>Furyborn</i>, one of my favorite books of the year). <br/><br/>As it turns out, <i>Sawkill Girls</i> wasn't for me. I considered raising my rating just for the sake of being polite. I didn't want other people to get discouraged fro</span>
  <span id="freeText11859879236823865533" style="display:none">RATING: 2.75 rounded up to 3/5 <br /><br />Let me start by saying that I LOVE horror. Spooky, creepy and bizarre is my aesthetic. Supernatural shows are my thing; I can't get enough of them. So, when I read this book's synopsis I was definitely intrigued. Plus, <b>Claire Legrand</b> is the author (she wrote <i>Furyborn</i>, one of my favorite books of the year). <br /><br />As it turns out, <i>Sawkill Girls</i> wasn't for me. I considered raising my rating just for the sake of being polite. I didn't want other people to get discouraged from reading this because of me. Later, I realized that I have to be honest and objective. My opinion might not be popular but that doesn't mean I shouldn't share it. <br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b><br />1) The LGBTQ representation was great. Asexuality is not often seen in YA. I'm happy with the way it was portrayed, it seemed very realistic. There's also a gay and a bisexual character.<br />2) The plot wasn't very original but it was solid. I'm certain that the author put a lot of thought into it and tried her best to make it unique. <br /><br /><b>What I didn't like:</b> <br />1) The pacing felt off. Stuff was happening but I didn't feel excited or intrigued. I hate using the term 'boring' but there isn't another way to describe it. <br />2) There were three main characters: Val, Zoey and Marion. I didn't like any of them. They seemed really plain and, once again, boring. None of them had much personality. The same could be said for all the side characters. <br />3) The tone of the story seemed to change. First it was magical and mysterious, then it got darker and then it just got weird (and not in an enjoyable way). I skimmed the last 30% because I just wanted it to be over. <br /><br /><b>In conclusion</b>, this wasn't my cup of tea but it could be yours! Most of the people who have read this rated it 4 or 5 stars. This was just my opinion. If the premise interests you, give this a shot.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11859879236823865533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3040014817" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tappkalina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="tappkalina" href="/user/show/32352828-tappkalina">tappkalina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=lgbt-read">lgbt-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3040014817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6982518127481389189"><blockquote>
  <b>“Why do the monsters eat girls?” she asked at last. Her voice sounded small. <br/>When Marion didn’t answer, Zoey turned on her side to face her. “Marion?” <br/>“Because,” Marion answered, looking beyond Zoey to the sea, “when a predator hunts, it seeks out the vulnerable. The desperate.”<br/>Zoey’s laugh was bitter. “Oh, and we poor delicate girls are vulnerable and desperate, is that what you’re saying?”<br/>“What I’m saying,” Marion said, now looking right at Zoey, her gray eyes bright, “is that girls hunger.</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6982518127481389189" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“Why do the monsters eat girls?” she asked at last. Her voice sounded small. <br>When Marion didn’t answer, Zoey turned on her side to face her. “Marion?” <br>“Because,” Marion answered, looking beyond Zoey to the sea, “when a predator hunts, it seeks out the vulnerable. The desperate.”<br>Zoey’s laugh was bitter. “Oh, and we poor delicate girls are vulnerable and desperate, is that what you’re saying?”<br>“What I’m saying,” Marion said, now looking right at Zoey, her gray eyes bright, “is that girls hunger. And we’re taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn’t enough food for us all.”</b>
</blockquote> <br>I actually dnf'd this a few months ago, but who can say no to a horror book with lesbians? Not me, that's for sure. <br>So I picked up the audiobook. <br>And it was a-ma-zing! The narrator is stunning.<br><br>It's not my genre, but I would say I liked the story. Although what made this one of my favourite reads this year are the characters. Every one of them.<br>I thought Marion is the new girl who figures thing out, Val is the evil queen bee and Zoey is the outcast; and that's it.<br>Wow, I was wrong. They are so much more than these stereotypes. <br>Marion lost so much, Val (probably my favourite character) doesn't and can't live her own life and Zoey is mad because no one believes her. Plus we have Grayson the cinnamon roll.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It also made me angry at so many levels. Like this:<br><blockquote>“God understands,” Briggs called out, “that these beasts are not supposed to be here. He has, in his wisdom, sent these girls to us. These girls whose power is contentious and self-defeating—except for in the hands of those strong enough to wield it. Our hands, my brothers. In our hands, these girls will be lifted up. Their sacrifice tonight will help us trap the beast while he is still bound to his queen. Their sacrifice tonight will ensure the safety of the world that depends on us to protect it.”</blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Lot of things that happened were so anti-women, but these girls sad: absolutely not! We sure as hell won't go down without a fight! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589408125ra/29470340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Or, in the case of the hunter men, we won't go down <i>with</i> a fight, because they wanted to force them to kill each other. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This one broke me:<br><blockquote>As she’d dressed in a set of Grayson’s old pinstriped pajamas, it had occurred to Zoey that Mrs. Althouse was hovering over them, making sure they ate and bathed, because she had no one left to mother.</blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
