<div id="review_2580105108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580105108" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580105108?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=feminist">feminist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=bi-mc">bi-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lesbian-mc">lesbian-mc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580105108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11735220534335042218">does anyone else feel like YA fantasy has been kinda dropping the ball lately? Because I'm here to report yet ANOTHER one has let me down and I don't know who to blame at this point. <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Beware the woods and the dark, dank, deep. He'll follow you home, and he won't let you sleep.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Sawkill Girls is a fantasy horror set on Sawkill Island - where an unusual and alarming amount of young girls go missing without a trace. No bodies, no word, no clues. When Zoey's best friend becomes the next missing </span>
  <span id="freeText11735220534335042218" style="display:none">does anyone else feel like YA fantasy has been kinda dropping the ball lately? Because I'm here to report yet ANOTHER one has let me down and I don't know who to blame at this point. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Beware the woods and the dark, dank, deep. He'll follow you home, and he won't let you sleep.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Sawkill Girls is a fantasy horror set on Sawkill Island - where an unusual and alarming amount of young girls go missing without a trace. No bodies, no word, no clues. When Zoey's best friend becomes the next missing girl - she decides it's time to find out what is happening on Sawkill once and for all. <br /><br />We follow three main characters, whose lives on the Island begin to intertwine as they confront the islands hidden secrets, and the evil that lurks in the shadows. <br /><br /><b>🌲 Zoey</b> Our main character - Island inhabitant who lost her best friend and wants to know what happened. Notoriously called out Val for stealing her best friend, and will do anything to find out what happened to her. She is asexual, black, and attracted to both girls and boys. Her father is also the town sheriff, and her ex Grayson plays a role in the book. <br /><br />🌲 <b>Valerie/Val</b> The islands queen bee who comes from a long line of wealthy women who live on the island. She has a secret and is part of a dark family legacy she cannot escape. She is also sapphic, but doesn't have a label. <br /><br />🌲 <b>Marion</b> A new comer to the island. She moves to Sawkill with her sister, but soon becomes embroiled with the mystery of Sawkill Island. She becomes friends with both Zoey and Val, and is part of an f/f relationship in this book. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Tragedy had touched Sawkill, again and again and again, but after each girl’s disappearance, once a respectable amount of time had passed, everyone seemed to stop caring.”<br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>First of all, there is plenty to like here</b>. Sawkill Girls is the spooky, atmospheric horror book that is perfect for cuddling down in bed with around Halloween. Legrand did a good job at constructing atmosphere here, and bringing a creepy aesthetic to the book - which included moth infested rooms, dark things crawling in the woods, scattered human body parts, demon children and plenty of blood, gore and trauma. There were parts of this book which genuinely creeped me out, especially those involving demon entities, and I really liked that this book managed to creep me out a little. <br /><br />I also really enjoyed the romances and relationships in this. The f/f relationship is WONDERFUL and I really loved how literally every character in this was sapphic. The romance was sweet and while it wasn't a major part of the story, it was there just enough to keep me happy and satisfied. The secondary relationship between Grayson and Zoey, which isn't really a romance but is more a friendship where they used to be exes was also GREAT. I love seeing exes in books because I feel it is so rare, and I adored their dynamic and friendship SO much. <br /><br /><u>But for me what just didn't work was the characters, and part two.</u> <br /><br />The characters were enjoyable to read about, but I didn't find myself particular invested in them. This may be because of the audiobook narrator, but I often found myself mixing them up and forgetting which one was which, and what their story or role was. Marion and Zoey especially I was getting mixed up. <br /><br />I also think part two of this book relied a lot on me being invested in and believed in their frienship as a trio which .. I wasn't feeling so much. While I think it was there, it didn't pull me in to the degree I would have liked, and I didn't feel convinced by what Legrand was putting down in this. <br /><br />I also found part two extremely predictable. While I loved the set up in part one, and the mystery elements, the second part didn't really stick the landing for me. The major plot points were obvious, and some felt a little cliche. There was really only one scene in part two I REALLY REALLY LOVED and the rest I just enjoyed, but didn't feel particularly strongly on. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls. All of them Sawkill girls.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>That all being said, I think this is a book many could love</b>. Even though I'm giving it a three star (which still means I liked it) I would 100% recommend it. This did have a really enjoyable set up and some great, creepy, atmospheric writing and scenes. The romances were wonderful, and there wasn't anything wrong with the plot - it just didn't grab me as much as I needed to rate it higher. But if you like creepy books - and if you liked books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a> or even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> I think you could definitely like this !<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11735220534335042218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2430004961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430004961" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2430004961?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38186306-sawkill-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2430004961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7459791436898800706">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/08/22/sawkill-girls-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/> <i>"Beware of the woods and the dark, dank deep.<br/><br/> He’ll follow you home, and he won’t let you sleep."</i><br/><br/>🌟 To do this book right I have to admit that I went into it not expecting a horror story and by no means it was one. But I was checking GR and searching online and I saw many readers listed it as a horror book but Edelweiss -Thanks for providing a copy in exchange of an honest review- did not, so my expectations kind of ch</span>
  <span id="freeText7459791436898800706" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/08/22/sawkill-girls-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /> <i>"Beware of the woods and the dark, dank deep.<br /><br /> He’ll follow you home, and he won’t let you sleep."</i><br /><br />🌟 To do this book right I have to admit that I went into it not expecting a horror story and by no means it was one. But I was checking GR and searching online and I saw many readers listed it as a horror book but Edelweiss -Thanks for providing a copy in exchange of an honest review- did not, so my expectations kind of changed while I was reading it which was kind of bad.<br /><br />🌟 This book started very good and then it lost some of the magic gradually till the end. I read 100 pages when I started this in one sitting which is something I don’t usually do. I heard mixed thing about Legrand writing but I found that I liked it… At least at the beginning.<br /><br />🌟 Toward the end what really happened is that I felt the author was trying so hard and it was kind of slow and boring, I usually speed through the last pages in all books because I want to know what happens and fast. I found myself wanting it to end here so I was reading, not caring what could happen. The problem is that many of the twists were revealed early in the book and every thing was clear from the start so the excitement factor dissipated early and it became kind of repetitive.<br /><br />🌟 I also found that it was kind of confusing at some points but I didn’t know if that was the book or if I wasn’t concentrating enough due to the boredom.<br /><br />🌟 That being said, it was not bad as to DNF or even considering doing so. I mean it was average to good but it had more potential for sure.<br /><br />🌟 This is also another book that has 3 girls as the main characters and it is feminine and empowers girls..etc which I am totally fine with. But what I am not totally fine with is that girls being powerful and great does not mean that all guys are bad and smelly and stupid. Both Genders can do anything. I am bothered by this concept that I touched in this book and IRL.<br /><br />🌟 Summary and prescription: A good book with a wide cast of female characters. It was also a LGBTQ diverse book with many different sexualities. Great for those looking for a feminine read.<br />And could have more potential in my opinion.<br /><br /> <i>“Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls. All of them Sawkill girls.”</i><br /><br />🌟 When I first started this I wanted to give it 4 stars, then it changed to 3.5 and after 2 days of reading I decided that 3.25 is the rating I am most comfortable with.</span>

<div id="review_2520587297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2520587297" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2520587297?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=reviewed-arcs">reviewed-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2520587297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1527340745258428128">Drop everything and add this to your October TBR's immediately.<br/><br/>If you like creepy, atmospheric books with badass females that keep you on the edge of your seat then look no further than <em>Sawkill Girls</em>. Earlier this year I read Claire Legrand's novel <em>Furyborn</em> and loved it. From her writing, to her characters, to her world-building I was instantly sucked into the story. So, naturally when I came across that the author was coming out with a new YA Fantasy/Horror novel with LGBT+ rep I couldn't add i</span>
  <span id="freeText1527340745258428128" style="display:none">Drop everything and add this to your October TBR's immediately.<br /><br />If you like creepy, atmospheric books with badass females that keep you on the edge of your seat then look no further than <em>Sawkill Girls</em>. Earlier this year I read Claire Legrand's novel <em>Furyborn</em> and loved it. From her writing, to her characters, to her world-building I was instantly sucked into the story. So, naturally when I came across that the author was coming out with a new YA Fantasy/Horror novel with LGBT+ rep I couldn't add it to my TBR fast enough. Now here we are, on publication day and all I can do scream from the rooftops about how good this was.<br /><br /><em>Sawkill Girls</em> is told through four different POV's and short chapters, which means you're going to have trouble putting this down. I absolutely adored all three of our leading ladies, Marion, Val, and Zoey. Three fierce feminists with three extraordinary powers. How could you not love them already? If you asked me to choose I honestly don't think I could give you a straight answer on who I loved more, but here's a quick rundown:<br /> <br />-Zoey, the driving force behind solving the mystery of the missing girls of Sawkill, is black and asexual with a backstory included. It was super nice to read Zoey's backstory instead of having the asexual rep dropped in just for the sake of including it. 10 points for you, Ms. Legrand.<br /><br />-Val, the queen bee, who reminded me so much of Jennifer from the movie <em>Jennifer's Body</em> is hoarding years and years worth of secrets kept by her family. It's mentioned in the story that she mainly dates boys, however, as the story progresses she beings to have feelings for one <br /><br />-Marion, the newbie to Sawkill, who is quickly losing her grip on what's real and what's not, is labeled as bisexual and fat. The fat rep is probably some of the best I've ever read. There's really no negativity towards Marion's size and I was <strong>LIVING</strong> for it. Marion's POV was always very interesting to read because as the story progressed you began to question if what she was experiencing was real or not.<br /> <br />And last but not least, our fourth POV...<br /><br /> <br />-The Rock. Yes, you read that right. Technically, a piece of land had a POV in this story and it was genius. The Rock's "<em>chapters</em>" were never more than a page or two, but it's POV was so beautifully written that it made this book even harder to put down.<br /> <br />On top of the awesome characters, we were also blessed with some great side characters. I <strong>LOVED</strong> Zoey's father and Grayson (Zoey's ex but still best friend). I was not let down one bit with the world building. If I didn't risk the chance of being abducted Sawkill would definitely be a place I would want to live, or at least visit. The creepy level in this was just the right amount too. At one point I actually had to put the book down because it was 1am and I heard some noises outside and was creeped the hell out. There were also a few times I physically shuddered while reading this. You can expect lots of bugs...and maybe even a little horse hair too. 😰<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls.<br /><em>All of them Sawkill girls.</em></em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“What I’m saying is that girls hunger. And we’re taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn’t enough food for us all.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Pain is pain. It's not a contest.</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>In New Jersey, it was the Jersey devil. On Sawkill Rock, it was the Collector.</em>
</blockquote><br />^ I thought this was interesting because most people don't talk about the Jersey Devil, but then I read that the author is from NJ and it made complete sense. Us Jersey girls gotta stick together.<br /><br />All in all, if you like creepy, atmospheric, feminist stories, <em>Sawkill Girls</em> is not one you want to pass up. Plus, I mean, it's not like you need to wait for the book to come out. Head on over to your bookstore today because <em>Sawkill Girls </em>is officially out on shelves ready to creep you the F out.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1527340745258428128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2188835644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188835644" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188835644?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188835644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9925480033036268091"><i>“Or maybe, Zoey thought darkly, legends about monsters weren’t so funny when girls were actually dying.”</i><br/><br/>We all have these unread books that we've been making love eyes at for years but somehow still never got around to reading them. Books where we just somehow know we're gonna end up liking them. This was <i>Sawkill Girls</i> for me. It gave me <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30249925.This_Darkness_Mine' title='This Darkness Mine by Mindy McGinnis' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Darkness Mine</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42505366.Wilder_Girls' title='Wilder Girls by Rory Power' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wilder Girls</a> vibes, two of my favourite books in recent years. Both were dark and gritty with complex, unlikeable female protagonists. Sa</span>
  <span id="freeText9925480033036268091" style="display:none"><i>“Or maybe, Zoey thought darkly, legends about monsters weren’t so funny when girls were actually dying.”</i><br /><br />We all have these unread books that we've been making love eyes at for years but somehow still never got around to reading them. Books where we just somehow know we're gonna end up liking them. This was <i>Sawkill Girls</i> for me. It gave me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30249925.This_Darkness_Mine" title="This Darkness Mine by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">This Darkness Mine</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42505366.Wilder_Girls" title="Wilder Girls by Rory Power" rel="nofollow noopener">Wilder Girls</a> vibes, two of my favourite books in recent years. Both were dark and gritty with complex, unlikeable female protagonists. Sawkill Girls did not end up meeting all my expectations. To be fair, the bar was set super high.<br /><br />Now, the beginning is the strongest part of the book. It sets the obscure, grim, unwelcoming mood and introduces three very different, very compelling main characters. Marion: grief-stricken und lonely. Zoey: ferocious and headstrong. Val: gorgeous and ice cold. A big plus is that all three girls are super queer. It promised to be a character-driven mystery novel...but it didn't fulfil that promise. The POVs started blending into each other, became messier, lost their strong individual voice. It turned out to be a fast-paced and plot-driven novel instead. Which isn't bad, I just prefer the former.<br /><br />Plotwise it is again an awesome setup that becomes messier the more it develops. The mystery aspect was soon lost because the many POVs tell us everything we want to know. There isn't really much left to discover after a while. I personally found the secret cult very stereotypical and cheap. It threw me off because it felt out of place and slightly illogical at the same time. Overall, I think it's a great concept (that inspired me to write my own dark island fantasy story) but the execution isn't as strong as I wished it were.<br /><br />Thumbs up for the very sapphic content and the discussion of asexuality. We don't get that in a lot of YA books (yet - I'm counting the minutes until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42115981.Loveless" title="Loveless by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Loveless</a> finally finds its way into my grabby hands).<br /><br />Three stars because even though it isn't the most convincing read, I still enjoyed the story and found it very enigmatic and sinister.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9925480033036268091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2385550677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385550677" />
    <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn"><img alt="Lea (drumsofautumn)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592339546p2/7285286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385550677?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea (drumsofautumn)" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn">Lea (drumsofautumn)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38186306-sawkill-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn?shelf=f-f-relationship">f-f-relationship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn?shelf=most-anticipated-2018">most-anticipated-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn?shelf=no-physical-copy-liked">no-physical-copy-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn?shelf=arcs-done">arcs-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385550677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12960236735145741113">♦ <a href='https://youtu.be/n0ep_iHI-KA' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>Video Review</b>
</a> ♦<br/><br/>This is such a strange little book and I had a hard time getting into it. I almost DNFed it, not because I thought it was bad but because I felt it wouldn't be for me. And the setting and storyline really wasn't for me.<br/>But <b>at its core this story is about feminism, female friendship, and love</b> and it made me super emotional.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Girls hunger. And we're taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn't enough food for us all.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Let's talk about diversity!<br/>Val</span>
  <span id="freeText12960236735145741113" style="display:none">♦ <a href="https://youtu.be/n0ep_iHI-KA" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Video Review</b>
</a> ♦<br /><br />This is such a strange little book and I had a hard time getting into it. I almost DNFed it, not because I thought it was bad but because I felt it wouldn't be for me. And the setting and storyline really wasn't for me.<br />But <b>at its core this story is about feminism, female friendship, and love</b> and it made me super emotional.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Girls hunger. And we're taught, from the moment our brains can take it, that there isn't enough food for us all.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />Let's talk about diversity!<br />Val is queer and has had relationships with guys and a relationship with a girl during the book. Marion is plus-size and also queer. It is stated that in the past she had crushes on both guys and girls. Zoey is black and asexual.<br /><br /><b>I loved all of the characters so much.</b> They really carried this novel for me. The three girls at the centre of this story are all so wonderful and so different. This is one of those stories where you can probably recognize yourself in at least one of them and I love that.<br />The way these girls work together and fight together, the way they work through their differences, through so much hard stuff keeping them apart, wanting them to fail.. it's honestly beautiful because all the odds are against them in so many ways. But they end up having the most wonderful friendship.<br />And while this book has a whole lot of shitty men in it, there is one male character, Grayson, Zoey's best friend and love interest, who was the sweetest soft boy in the whole world and I wanna protect him at all costs. The relationship between him and Zoey was lovely and talked about some really important aspects.<br /><br />There is also a beautiful, so so so sossososoooo beautiful f/f romance in this book. I don't have words for how beautiful. <b>This relationship meant a whole bunch to me and I think it's gonna mean a whole bunch for a lot of (teenage) girls out there.</b> Bless praise Twenty GayTeen!<br />This also features one of the best sex scenes in YA. The fact that we are living in a time where we get the gift of such a well-written, non-explicit sex scene between two girls in YA left me absolutely speechless.<br /><br />I would say the ace representation was overall well done and there was such an important conversation around it, but if you are on the ace-spectrum yourself, please tread carefully. There is one huge acephobic statement in this book and while it was immediately challenged and apologized for, I know this is gonna be hard to read for some people.<br />There are A LOT of other triggers in this book and I honestly couldn't even catch them all but here are some <b>trigger and content warnings:</b> murder (and pretty gruesome ones), blood, gore, parental abuse, violence, sexual abuse and honestly the threat of sexual assault just kinda hangs in the air constantly.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You are a small girl. You are mighty. You are fragile. You can move mountains. You are breakable. You will never break.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />I think this book is absolutely perfect if you're looking for a creepy read for October that is a little different. It will creep you the fuck out but it will also make you feel a lot of good things.<br />Ultimately for me this book didn't score because of it's atmosphere, setting, storyline or pretty writing but simply because of how it celebrated girls. How it shows that we are stronger together, better together. Society can tell us all they want about what we are supposed to be and how we are supposed to feel, but <b>if we stick together, we are the strongest fucking force out there.</b><br /><br />♦ <a href="https://www.youtube.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Channel</a> ♦ <a href="https://twitter.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♦ <a href="https://instagram.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♦<br /><br /><i>I received an ARC of this through Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12960236735145741113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2358704331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358704331" />
    <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos"><img alt="Julie Zantopoulos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503178209p2/51094260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358704331?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Zantopoulos" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos">Julie Zantopoulos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062696625" href="/book/show/36339614-sawkill-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=diverse-read">diverse-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358704331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8211670868651456683">Claire's writing is beautiful, there's no denying that, but this story just didn't connect for me. Let's chat about the premise of this book: <br/><br/>Girls on Sawkill island have been disappearing for generations and island legend warns of a Collector who steals away said girls and does heaven knows what with them...but they're never seen again. Then three girls come into magical mystical powers and battle a deep dark evil that only they have the power to vanquish. Sounds pretty badass and spooky...righ</span>
  <span id="freeText8211670868651456683" style="display:none">Claire's writing is beautiful, there's no denying that, but this story just didn't connect for me. Let's chat about the premise of this book: <br /><br />Girls on Sawkill island have been disappearing for generations and island legend warns of a Collector who steals away said girls and does heaven knows what with them...but they're never seen again. Then three girls come into magical mystical powers and battle a deep dark evil that only they have the power to vanquish. Sounds pretty badass and spooky...right?<br /><br />The atmosphere of this book had potential but fell flat for me. I blame <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2279692253" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked Deep</a> which ruined me for all atmospheric island settings, honestly. This one features wild horses (that play an odd magical roll) and cliffs/underground caverns and woods that should be more vibrant than they end up being. The lighthouse is the only feature of the island that stood out to me, often called The Eye ala Lord of the Rings. Otherwise, the setting fell really flat for me. <br /><br />Characters: <br /><br />Zoey: Our African-American ace badass. She's lost a best friend, her father is the Sheriff and she somehow landed the love of the sweetest most amazing guy, ever. She's pretty great, tbh. I love that there is on the page ace representation and discussions!<br /><br />Marion: She just lost her father, her sister is taken by the Collector, and her world is shattering as she lands on Sawkill island and is immediately struck with migraines and illness as The Rock speaks to her. We never learn a ton about her as a character outside of her being the strong one of her family and a beautifully bi character in an f/f relationship inside this book. PS-her father is a tool whose actions make no damn sense. <br /><br />Val: Her family is tied to The Collector and she's had the shit end of the stick. You hate her, love her, hate her, and then cry for her. She's got a pretty awesome arc and some fantastic lines about claiming one's own body and mind for themselves. She's kinda amazing, tbh.<br /><br />Grayson: Zoey's love interest is a sweet baby angel and needs to be protected at all cost...you will love him.<br /><br />The Collector: started off pretty freaking creepy and ended up campy and utterly unscary. Supposedly an otherworldly shapeshifting evil bonded to a family of females who bind him to this realm...he mates with them, makes them bring him kills, and generally is evil. Yet, somehow, he becomes a laughable and forgettable villain. <br /><br />The Rock: The island literally is a character in this book and possibly one of the best ones in the entire book. It was a pretty unique POV that I really enjoyed. <br /><br />The Hand of Light: Legit a male centered cult/society whose job it is to vanquish these monsters by sacrificing young girls. Yeah, that's a thing. They're a**holes.<br /><br />The plot meandered a bit, there was great romances in the book, great discussions about sexuality and family but oh man did it go from legit spooky to bad Scooby Doo writing. Once the Hand of Light came in, I was out. While they serve as a catalyst for some seriously badass feminist quotes in the book and stand as a metaphor for women taking down the patriarchy...it was just too campy for me. What could have been a really powerful message was outweighed by how little sense they made. It all could have been handled so much better, honestly. <br /><br />People die in this book and for the most part, they stay dead. I can appreciate that. People get angry for things people say/do and aren't easily forgiven. There are discussions about shitty behavior and how to make up for it if they can ever make up for it, and that's great. There's no clean "all is well" crap when people mess up and I love that. It's real and raw and messy but still, something just did not connect with me. It was an okay read but it could have been so much more. <br /><br />I read this with my friends on June 9th! Can't wait to discuss this with them and read something else by Claire! Arc acquired at BookCon.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13507409-amy …" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside …" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17590369-imogen-gray …" rel="nofollow noopener">Imogen</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf …" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellie</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35673299-laura-yamin …" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68321894-natasha …" rel="nofollow noopener">Natasha</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42780417-wren-wrensreads …" rel="nofollow noopener">Wren</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36907106-alexis-theslothreader …" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexis</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3030788-melanie …" rel="nofollow noopener">Melanie</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8211670868651456683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2586735374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2586735374" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2586735374?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=dark-fiction">dark-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586735374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4151326076400069451">“Theirs was not a world that was often kind to women.”<br/><br/>I read the Sawkills Girls for the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/group_folder/385108' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goodreads Ladies of Horror Fiction discussion. </a><br/><br/>Sawkill Girls is the story of three teenage girls who come together to face an ancient evil. It’s also about friendships and families and duty and the daily aches and pains and confusion that teenagers face.<br/><br/>Marion, her sister and her mom have relocated to Sawkill to start a new life after the death of the girls’ father. Sawkill is an isolated place inhabited by m</span>
  <span id="freeText4151326076400069451" style="display:none">“Theirs was not a world that was often kind to women.”<br /><br />I read the Sawkills Girls for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/group_folder/385108" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads Ladies of Horror Fiction discussion. </a><br /><br />Sawkill Girls is the story of three teenage girls who come together to face an ancient evil. It’s also about friendships and families and duty and the daily aches and pains and confusion that teenagers face.<br /><br />Marion, her sister and her mom have relocated to Sawkill to start a new life after the death of the girls’ father. Sawkill is an isolated place inhabited by mostly wealthy people but Marion seems ready to start anew but things go so terrible wrong. <br /><br />Zoey’s best friend is one of many girls who have disappeared on Sawkill. Zoey isn’t towing the line spouted by the residents who aren’t terribly alarmed by the disappearance. They assume she fell off a cliff and leave it at that. Zoey won’t let things go even when her police officer father insists she must. She snoops and she sniffs out trouble!<br /><br />Val is the town beauty. The high school Queen Bee whose “smile was made of diamonds and bee stings”. Everyone falls under Val’s spell except for Zoey. Zoey blames Val for the loss of her missing friend.<br /><br />So those are the girls. How they interact and the things that are uncovered make up the rest of the story and I was hooked for the first 2/3’s. There were some truly creeptastic scenes here, especially those with the devilish little “boy”. The atmosphere is also fantastic. The island breathes dread, drips spiders (ahhh!) and the reader is kept off kilter for quite a bit. I loved that. The writing is engaging and the characters are multi-faceted and, best of all, no one person is terrible and no one person is perfect. I loved that too. The only thing that I didn’t love was the insta-love relationship between two of the characters that seemed to have no believable build-up beforehand. I get it. They’re teens and lust happens but this didn’t feel real. Give us a little build-up first! There wasn’t any attraction noted before the big kiss. That always bugs me and feels like a cheat.<br /><br />Somewhere around the 2/3 mark things started to drag for me. I’m guessing it’s because the action took over and I’m not a huge action fan so this is on me and my personal preferences. I’d easily recommend it to someone looking for a young adult horror novel with well-drawn characters. I'm giving it a three which means "I liked it" according to the Goodreads scale up there so please don't try to change my opinion in the comments which seems to happen on most of my 3 star reviews because I will get grouchy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4151326076400069451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2599608820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2599608820" />
    <a title="Karima chermiti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti"><img alt="Karima chermiti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521752993p2/42944800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2599608820?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karima chermiti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karima chermiti" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti">Karima chermiti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062696625" href="/book/show/36339614-sawkill-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=theme-thieves-november_2018">theme-thieves-november_2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2599608820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5713922498410457319"><br/><b>Actual rating : 2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>What could I say about this one, I don’t know, I’m deeply confused? I can’t seem to be able to make up my mind about this book and honestly it’s annoying me. This book belongs to that area when I don’t love a book and I don’t hate it either, I feel no attachment to it and yet it’s stuck on my mind. But to be fair, it’s stuck in my mind because of all of the weird shit that was happening and wasn’t properly explained. It felt like a vision or a dream sequence. It was odd.</span>
  <span id="freeText5713922498410457319" style="display:none"><br><b>Actual rating : 2.5 stars</b><br><br>What could I say about this one, I don’t know, I’m deeply confused? I can’t seem to be able to make up my mind about this book and honestly it’s annoying me. This book belongs to that area when I don’t love a book and I don’t hate it either, I feel no attachment to it and yet it’s stuck on my mind. But to be fair, it’s stuck in my mind because of all of the weird shit that was happening and wasn’t properly explained. It felt like a vision or a dream sequence. It was odd.<br><br>I’ve just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38198209-the-deepest-roots" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deepest Roots</a> and I find Sawkill Girls quite similar to it. I mean let’s break it down :<br><br>	Both books revolves around three female characters who are not what they seem to be<br>	Both books explores female friendship in its beauty and complexity<br>	Both books gives the female characters space to reveal themselves to the readers and it’s all about female empowerment and girls standing together and supporting each other which is great <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>A girl with incredible strength.<br>A girl who can vanish.<br>A girl who burns.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But here’s where both diverge, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38198209-the-deepest-roots" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deepest Roots</a> has more meaningful and believable relationships between its female characters and they feel more grounded in reality for me. I certainly loved them more than Val, Marion and Zoey. Also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38198209-the-deepest-roots" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deepest Roots</a> didn’t dwell too much on its weird shit and focused more on the human relationships while Sawkill girls gave us good dynamics but they felt rushed and the nonsensical things that were happening didn’t make sense at times. The supernatural in deepest roots was explained in a classic yet convincing way whereas in Sawkill girls, the author throw things at you and doesn’t bother to come up with something good.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Decades of dead girls. Poor girls and rich girls. Black and brown and white girls.<br>All of them Sawkill girls.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>In other terms, if you’re looking for a book about meaningful female relationships and great character arcs, maybe you’d want to read the deepest roots before this one, in my opinion.</i><br><br><b>But let’s stop with the comparisons and focus more on the Sawkill girls.</b><br><br>My main problem with this book is that the things that were great about it from one angle were totally bothersome from another one. Take for an example the female relationship in this book; it is complex, strong and beautifully intense but it develops too quickly and it doesn’t give you the time to take it in or appreciate it. <br><br>The romance was another thing that was done well in this book but was it? I’m torn about this element because it’s an f/f romance and we don’t see a lot of those in YA books so I appreciate that it exists and I love that it felt true and liberating for both characters but it develops suddenly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One minute, Val and Marion are strangers and the next they’re in love just because they happen to have a heart to heart talking. It also made me feel like Marion really didn’t give a shit about her sister or what was happening, the Timing was off considering the circumstances that brought them together, I felt like “ we know that girls are dying in gruesome ways all over and maybe you got my sister killed but let’s make out” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m sorry as much as I appreciate the romance, it makes Marion character’s feel inconsistent, like she talks all the time about doing anything for her sister but when her sister disappear she is more focusing on her blossoming relationship with Val than finding her sister which doesn’t make sense to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Everything great about this book is followed by a BUT. The dynamics were captivating but they needed more time to develop naturally. The romance was appreciated and it made complete sense for Val and Marion to be drawn to each other but considering the circumstances surrounding it, it left me feeling cold.<br><br>Also, did anyone notice those little comments especially at the end of the book about men and how they’re all assholes like at every chance the author got? You know I love the fact that it’s a book about girl power and about women fighting to change their lives and to take matters in their own hands but we don’t have to view every single man as the enemy to achieve that. <br><br>I feel like I kept talking only about the bad things, in my defense, they’re many but let’s talk about something that I really loved, Zoey’s character, her arc and her representation as an asexual black girl. I loved Zoey’s chapters so much and I loved her spirit and how consistent her character felt through the whole book. she was my favorite character in the entire book and her relationship with her boyfriend/best friend is so good and it evolved and grew in a convincing way.<br><br>I know that this book has a great spirit and the positive things it tried to portray are things that I support wholeheartedly but it had some glaring problems too. Bummer, it could’ve been a favorite.<br><br>but let's end this review on a positive note with this great quote <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You must keep fighting.<br>You must never stop fighting.<br>You must light the path for others to find their footing</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>********************************</b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book is exhausting <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543429608ra/26661787.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <i>Rating and Review to come cause I'm too drained to do anything.</i>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2469822579" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469822579" />
    <a title="andrea caro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33199497-andrea-caro"><img alt="andrea caro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465427029p2/33199497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2469822579?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="andrea caro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="andrea caro" href="/user/show/33199497-andrea-caro">andrea caro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=girls-girls-girls">girls-girls-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=favorites-2018">favorites-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33199497-andrea-caro?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2469822579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17128033455110298451">First of all, I want to give a very enthusiastic thank you to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14843185.Julie_Zantopoulos' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julie</a> for sending me this ARC. Not only was this one of two most anticipated reads of the year for me, she also left in her tabs color-coded to thematic elements in the story so this reading experience was kind of incredible and revolutionary for me.<br/><br/>Now, onto the review:<br/><br/>This book is spooky, queer, feminist, and full of women and I loved it. This story follows around several points of view, three of which are Zoey, Marion, and Val. Zoe</span>
  <span id="freeText17128033455110298451" style="display:none">First of all, I want to give a very enthusiastic thank you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14843185.Julie_Zantopoulos" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie</a> for sending me this ARC. Not only was this one of two most anticipated reads of the year for me, she also left in her tabs color-coded to thematic elements in the story so this reading experience was kind of incredible and revolutionary for me.<br /><br />Now, onto the review:<br /><br />This book is spooky, queer, feminist, and full of women and I loved it. This story follows around several points of view, three of which are Zoey, Marion, and Val. Zoey is black, bi, and asexual, grieving the disappearance of her friend Thora. Marion, new to the island, is grieving the death of her father and trying to hold her family together, and starts a relationship with another girl. Val has dark secrets and dates boys, but shows attraction to/begins a relationship with a female. Interestingly enough, there are chapters written in the point of view of the island itself; this sounds kooky but it's actually really interesting and worked well for me.<br /><br />Sawkill Island is an island where girls have gone missing over the past century or so. Over the past few years, the number of disappearances has been increasing. Things really start to escalate when Marion, her mom, and her sister move to the island to escape grief and pretty soon after, Marion's sister goes missing. Marion's journey ends up being about grief, being a parent to a parent acting like a child, then accepting shitty circumstances when backed up into a corner; Marion did whatever it took to survive and help out fellow women.<br /><br />Zoey felt, to me, like a Lois Lane-type character, really spearheading the mystery behind the missing girls, particularly after her best friend Thora goes missing, just after cozying up to Val. She's got an ex named Grayson who is cute as a fucking button, but it's interesting to read about why they didn't work out. Zoey feels shamed and is shamed for her asexuality (fyi - this is immediately corrected on page; it also felt really good to read the word 'asexual' on page and have it clearly established that asexuality and romance aren't mutually exclusive things). <br /><br />Val's story is dark, dark, dark, and hard to explain without going into too much detail. She isn't a squeaky-clean character, but for me she was necessary, exploring the nuances of what it's like to be a woman to be manipulated by men and other women for the sake of a man. <br /><br />One point - I wasn't necessarily on board for the f/f romance for a big part of this book, but I very much loved it at the end.<br /><br />The villain(s) in this book were pretty mysterious to start off with which left the first half of the book much more atmospheric. I understand the criticisms of them made in other reviews, but as 'cheesy' as both entities turned out to be, I felt it was the right choice for this book because it was about the women, not about the men that were torturing them. There were so many little snippets in this story that felt like something I've experienced from men because I'm female that I can't really unpack them all, but this book is pretty solidly feminist and I felt seen while reading a lot of the book.<br /><br />So anyway, so far I'd call this my favorite read of the year.<br /><br />Read this if you like:<br />- Spooky, atmospheric vibes<br />- Women <br />- Magic <br /><br />TW for: grief pertaining to loss of a loved one, gore, blood, abuse including parental, talk of miscarriages, a really ace-phobic comment that was immediately rebuffed on page, animal death, and at least discussion of sex abuse/rape.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17128033455110298451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VaIRr1pdIW0hQdVC9fR5cqQUHiaashrwG9fvh+dVL+5vBVQlMYpCVb+PJVBVQYqLJjFaasV/+kk0uST0OS17QQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MlYPKFq4zvoUojTxSxGs4GBNBaY+7LFLBWRgI3UFzY8I8UqiMW+twopsxOPrpF8Z4mhB6mEhUfIqCqtQq32ZIA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1074989.Claire_Legrand">About Claire Legrand</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1074989.Claire_Legrand"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1471747101p3/1074989.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1074989.Claire_Legrand">Claire Legrand

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15400367261905221037">Claire Legrand used to be a musician until she realized she couldn’t stop thinking about the stories in her head. Now she is a librarian and New York Times bestselling author living in central New Jersey.<br/><br/>Her first novel is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10893214.THE_CAVENDISH_HOME_FOR_BOYS_AND_GIRLS' title='THE CAVENDISH HOME FOR BOYS AND GIRLS' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE CAVENDISH HOME FOR BOYS AND GIRLS</a>, one of the New York Public Library’s 100 Titles for Reading and Sharing in 2012. She is also the author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13129136.THE_YEAR_OF_SHADOWS' title='THE YEAR OF SHADOWS' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE YEAR OF SHADOWS</a>, a ghost st</span>
  <span id="freeText15400367261905221037" style="display:none">Claire Legrand used to be a musician until she realized she couldn’t stop thinking about the stories in her head. Now she is a librarian and New York Times bestselling author living in central New Jersey.<br /><br />Her first novel is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10893214.THE_CAVENDISH_HOME_FOR_BOYS_AND_GIRLS" title="THE CAVENDISH HOME FOR BOYS AND GIRLS" rel="nofollow noopener">THE CAVENDISH HOME FOR BOYS AND GIRLS</a>, one of the New York Public Library’s 100 Titles for Reading and Sharing in 2012. She is also the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13129136.THE_YEAR_OF_SHADOWS" title="THE YEAR OF SHADOWS" rel="nofollow noopener">THE YEAR OF SHADOWS</a>, a ghost story for middle grade readers; and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18475593.WINTERSPELL" title="WINTERSPELL" rel="nofollow noopener">WINTERSPELL</a>, a young adult re-telling of The Nutcracker. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260524.SOME_KIND_OF_HAPPINESS" title="SOME KIND OF HAPPINESS" rel="nofollow noopener">SOME KIND OF HAPPINESS</a>, her middle grade novel about mental illness, family secrets, and the power of storytelling, is a 2017 Edgar Award Nominee. Claire’s latest middle grade novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24565517.FOXHEART" title="FOXHEART" rel="nofollow noopener">FOXHEART</a>, is a classic fantasy-adventure and a 2016 Junior Library Guild selection. She is one of the four authors behind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8507023.THE_CABINET_OF_CURIOSITIES" title="THE CABINET OF CURIOSITIES" rel="nofollow noopener">THE CABINET OF CURIOSITIES</a>, an anthology of dark middle grade short fiction that was a Junior Library Guild selection, a Bank Street Best Book, and among the New York Public Library’s 100 Titles for Reading and Sharing in 2014.<br /><br />Her fantasy novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34323570.FURYBORN" title="FURYBORN" rel="nofollow noopener">FURYBORN</a> debuted at #4 on the New York Times bestseller list, and is the first book in the Empirium Trilogy, a young adult epic fantasy series. The next book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40523458.KINGSBANE" title="KINGSBANE" rel="nofollow noopener">KINGSBANE</a>, was also an instant New York Times bestseller. The third and final book in the trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36253143.LIGHTBRINGER" title="LIGHTBRINGER" rel="nofollow noopener">LIGHTBRINGER</a>, releases October 13, 2020.<br /><br />Her latest standalone book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38139409.SAWKILL_GIRLS" title="SAWKILL GIRLS" rel="nofollow noopener">SAWKILL GIRLS</a>, is a queer young adult horror novel that received five starred reviews. It is also a 2018 Bram Stoker Award finalist and a 2019 Lambda Literary Award finalist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15400367261905221037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
